Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural Catholic">Cultural Catholic</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Related ethnic groups</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gypsy_and_Traveller_groups" title="Scottish Gypsy and Traveller groups">Scottish traveller groups</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Irish Travellers</b> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">an lucht si\xc3\xbail</i>, meaning \'the walking people\') are a traditionally <a href="/wiki/Itinerant_groups_in_Europe" title="Itinerant groups in Europe">itinerant</a> ethnic group who maintain a set of traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QuestioningGypsy_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuestioningGypsy-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Although predominantly English-speaking, some also use <a href="/wiki/Shelta" title="Shelta">Shelta</a> and other similar <a href="/wiki/Cant_(language)" title="Cant (language)">cants</a>. They live mostly in <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> as well as comprising large communities in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Their origin is disputed. Traveller rights groups have long pushed for ethnic status from the Irish government, finally succeeding in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The historical origins of Irish Travellers as a group has been a subject of academic and popular debate. Research is complicated by the fact that the group has no written records of its own.<sup id="cite_ref-Solidaritywith_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solidaritywith-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2016)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> They might be of <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani</a> extraction, although this theory is disputed and theories of pre-Gaelic origin also exist.<sup id="cite_ref-Keane2005_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keane2005-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>43</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jean-Pierre_Li%C3%A9geois&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jean-Pierre Li\xc3\xa9geois (page does not exist)">Jean-Pierre Li\xc3\xa9geois</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Li%C3%A9geois" class="extiw" title="fr:Jean-Pierre Li\xc3\xa9geois">fr</a>)</span> wrote that the Irish Traveller <a href="/wiki/Shelta" title="Shelta">Gammon</a> <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">vocabulary</a> is derived from pre-13th-century Gaelic <a href="/wiki/Idiom" title="Idiom">idioms</a> with ten percent Indian origin <a href="/wiki/Romani_language" title="Romani language">Romani language</a> vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Gaelic language expert <a href="/wiki/Kuno_Meyer" title="Kuno Meyer">Kuno Meyer</a> and Romani language linguist <a href="/wiki/John_Sampson_(linguist)" title="John Sampson (linguist)">John Sampson</a> both asserted that Shelta existed as far back as the 13th century, 300 years before the first Romani populations arrived in Ireland or Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (December 2015)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (November 2016)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint selfreference">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Talk:Irish_Travellers#Meyer_1909" title="Talk:Irish Travellers">discuss</a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Their origin is genetically Irish<sup id="cite_ref-ncbi.nlm.nih.gov_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncbi.nlm.nih.gov-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> with around 10,000 people in the United States being descendants of Travellers who left Ireland, mostly between 1845 and 1860 during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Great Famine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> About 2,500 of them live in <a href="/wiki/Murphys_Estates,_South_Carolina" title="Murphys Estates, South Carolina">Murphy Village</a>, a community outside <a href="/wiki/North_Augusta,_South_Carolina" title="North Augusta, South Carolina">North Augusta, South Carolina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, researchers at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Surgeons_in_Ireland" title="Royal College of Surgeons in Ireland">Royal College of Surgeons</a> in Dublin and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a> analyzed DNA samples from 40 Travellers. The study provided evidence that Irish Travellers are a distinct Irish ethnic minority, who separated from the settled Irish community at least 1000 years ago; the report claimed that they are as distinct from the settled community as <a href="/wiki/Icelanders" title="Icelanders">Icelanders</a> are from <a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Irish Travellers "left no written record of their own" and their families do not date back to the same time; some families adopted Traveller customs centuries ago, while others did so more recently.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> It is unclear how many Irish Travellers would be included in this distinct ethnic group from a genetic perspective.\n</p><p>Among other speculation on their origins, "two theories are rejected outright": that they were descended from those Irish who were made homeless by <a href="/wiki/Cromwellian_conquest_of_Ireland" title="Cromwellian conquest of Ireland">Oliver Cromwell\'s military campaign in Ireland in the 1650s</a>, or made homeless in the <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Hunger" class="mw-redirect" title="The Great Hunger">1840s famine</a> due to eviction.<sup id="cite_ref-Keane2005_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keane2005-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>56</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_genetics">Population genetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Population genetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>A genetic analysis of Irish Travellers found evidence to support the hypotheses of: (1) Irish ancestry; (2) several distinct subpopulations; and (3) the distinctiveness of the midland counties due to Viking influence.<sup id="cite_ref-ncbi.nlm.nih.gov_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncbi.nlm.nih.gov-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Genetic studies by Miriam Murphy, David Croke, and other researchers identified certain genetic diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Galactosemia" title="Galactosemia">galactosemia</a> that are more common in the Irish Traveller population, involving identifiable <a href="/wiki/Allele" title="Allele">allelic</a> mutations that are rarer among the rest of the community.\n</p><p>Two main hypotheses have arisen, speculating whether:\n</p>\n<ol><li>this resulted from marriages made largely within and among the Traveller community, or</li>\n<li>suggesting descent from an <a href="/wiki/Founder_effect" title="Founder effect">original Irish carrier</a> long ago with ancestors unrelated to the rest of the Irish population.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>\n<p>They concluded that: "The fact that Q188R is the sole mutant allele among the Travellers as compared to the non-Traveller group may be the result of a <a href="/wiki/Founder_effect" title="Founder effect">founder effect</a> in the isolation of a small group of the Irish population from their peers as founders of the Traveller sub-population. This would favour the second, endogenous, hypothesis of Traveller origins."\n</p><p>More specifically, they found that Q188R was found in 100% of Traveller samples, and in 89% of other Irish samples, indicating that the Traveller group was typical of the larger Irish indigenous population.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_commissions_on_Irish_Travellers">Government commissions on Irish Travellers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Government commissions on Irish Travellers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_17th_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 17th D\xc3\xa1il">1959\xe2\x80\x9363 government of Ireland</a> established a "Commission on Itinerancy" with the following terms of reference:<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196311_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196311-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>(1) to enquire into the problem arising from the presence in the country of itinerants in considerable numbers;</dd>\n<dd>(2) to examine the economic, educational, health and social problems inherent in their way of life;</dd>\n<dd>(3) to consider what steps might be taken\xe2\x80\x94\n<dl><dd>(a) to provide opportunities for a better way of life for itinerants,</dd>\n<dd>(b) to promote their absorption into the general community,</dd>\n<dd>(c) pending such absorption, to reduce to a minimum the disadvantages to themselves and to the community resulting from their itinerant habits and</dd>\n<dd>(d) to improve the position generally; and</dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>(4) to make recommendations.</dd></dl>\n<p>The Commission\'s 1963 report defined "itinerant" as "a person who had no fixed place of abode and habitually wandered from place to place, but excluding <a href="/wiki/Carny" title="Carny">travelling show-people</a> and travelling entertainers".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196312_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196312-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> It recommended <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">assimilation</a> of travellers by settling them in fixed dwellings, viewing the Netherlands\' approach to its travelling minority as a model.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196328,_106_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196328,_106-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> At the time, about 60% Irish travellers lived in barrel-roofed horse-drawn wagons, with almost 40% still using tents in summer (fewer in winter).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196340_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECommission_on_Itinerancy196340-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-heeujoc_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heeujoc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Travelling People Review Body (1981\xe2\x80\x9383) advocated <a href="/wiki/Social_integration" title="Social integration">integration</a> rather than assimilation,<sup id="cite_ref-heeujoc_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heeujoc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> with provision for serviced halting sites. The Body\'s membership included travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The Task Force on the Travelling Community (1993\xe2\x80\x9395) moved to an <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">intercultural</a> paradigm.<sup id="cite_ref-heeujoc_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heeujoc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Irish Travellers speak English and sometimes one of two dialects of <a href="/wiki/Shelta" title="Shelta">Shelta</a>, Gammon (or Gamin) and Irish Traveller Cant. Shelta has been dated back to the 18th century, but may be older.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cant_(language)" title="Cant (language)">Cant</a>, which derives from <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, is a combination of English and Shelta.<sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1996_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1996-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nomenclature">Nomenclature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Nomenclature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Travellers refer to themselves as <i>Minkiers</i><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> or <i>Pavees</i>, or in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> as <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">an Lucht Si\xc3\xbail</i> ("the travelling people").\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pejorative_names">Pejorative names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Pejorative names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Travellers are often referred to by the terms <i><a href="/wiki/Tinker" title="Tinker">tinkers</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Gipsies" class="mw-redirect" title="Gipsies">gipsies</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gypsie" class="mw-redirect" title="Gypsie">gypsies</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Itinerant_groups_in_Europe" title="Itinerant groups in Europe">itinerants</a></i>, or, pejoratively, <i><a href="/wiki/Knacker" title="Knacker">knackers</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Mulcahy2012_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mulcahy2012-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Some of these terms refer to services that were traditionally provided by the group: tinkering or tinsmithing, for example, being the mending of tinware such as pots and pans, and knackering being the acquisition of dead or old <a href="/wiki/Horse_slaughter" title="Horse slaughter">horses for slaughter</a>. The term <i>gypsy</i> first appears in records dating back to the 16th century when it was originally used to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental</a> <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Romani people</a> in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, who were mistakenly thought to be <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Okely1983_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okely1983-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p158</span>)</sup> Other derogatory names for itinerant groups have been used to refer to Travellers including the word <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pikey" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:pikey">pikey</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The 2016 census in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> reported the number of Irish Travellers as 30,987, up from 29,495 in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-2016CensusReport6_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016CensusReport6-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In 2006 the number was 22,369.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> A further 1,700 to 2,000 were estimated to live in <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the 2006 Irish census it was determined that 20,975 dwell in urban areas and 1,460 were living in rural areas. With an overall population of just 0.5% some areas were found to have a higher proportion, with Travellers constituting 7.71% of the population in <a href="/wiki/Tuam" title="Tuam">Tuam, Galway</a>. There were found to be 9,301 Travellers in the 0\xe2\x80\x9314 age range, comprising 41.5% of the Traveller population, and a further 3,406 of them were in the 15\xe2\x80\x9324 age range, comprising 15.2%. Children of age range 0\xe2\x80\x9317 comprised 48.7% of the Traveller population.\n</p><p>Following the findings of the All Ireland Traveller Health Study (estimates for 2008), the figure for Northern Ireland was revised to 3,905 and that for the Republic to 36,224.<sup id="cite_ref-Abdalla2010_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdalla2010-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Diaspora">Diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Britain">Great Britain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Great Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2011, for the first time, the census category "Irish Traveller" was introduced as part of the broader Gypsy/Traveller section. The self reported figure for collective Gypsy/Traveller and/or Irish Traveller populations were 63,193<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> but recent estimates of Travellers living in Great Britain range between 15,000<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> as part of a total estimation of 300,000 Romani and other Traveller groups in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/London_Boroughs" class="mw-redirect" title="London Boroughs">London Boroughs</a> of <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Harrow" title="London Borough of Harrow">Harrow</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Brent" title="London Borough of Brent">Brent</a> contain significant Irish Traveller populations. In addition to those on various official sites there are a number who are settled in local authority housing. These are mostly women who wish their children to have a chance at a good education. They and the children may or may not travel in the summer but remain in close contact with the wider Traveller community.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are also a number of Irish Traveller communities in the <a href="/wiki/Home_Counties" class="mw-redirect" title="Home Counties">Home Counties</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>There are no official population figures regarding Irish Travellers in the United States as the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census" title="United States Census">US census</a> does not recognise them as an ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1992_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1992-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1996_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1996-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>  While some sources estimate their population in the US to be 10,000, others suggest their population is 40,000. According to research published in 1992, Irish travellers in the US divide themselves up into groups that are based on historical residence: Ohio Travellers, Georgia Travellers, Texas Travellers, and Mississippi Travellers. The Georgia Travelers\' camp is made up of about eight hundred families, the Mississippi Travelers, about three hundred families, and the Texas Travelers, under fifty families."<sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1992_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1992-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1996_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1996-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest and most affluent population of about 2,500 lives in Murphy Village, outside of the town of <a href="/wiki/North_Augusta,_South_Carolina" title="North Augusta, South Carolina">North Augusta, South Carolina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Other communities exist in <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis, Tennessee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hernando,_Mississippi" title="Hernando, Mississippi">Hernando, Mississippi</a>, and near <a href="/wiki/White_Settlement,_Texas" title="White Settlement, Texas">White Settlement, Texas</a>, where the families stay in their homes during the winter, and leave during the summer, while smaller enclaves can be found across Georgia, Alabama, and Mississippi.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Travellers in the US are said to speak English and <a href="/wiki/Shelta" title="Shelta">Shelta</a>, a form of Cant. The Cant spoken in the US is similar to the Cant spoken in Ireland, but differs in some respects in that the language has transformed into a type of <a href="/wiki/Pidgin" title="Pidgin">pidgin</a> English over the generations. They typically work in asphalting, spray-painting, laying linoleum, or as itinerant workers to earn their living.<sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1992_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1992-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Andereck1996_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Andereck1996-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Travellers have a distinctive approach to religion; the vast majority are practising <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholics">Roman Catholics</a> with particular attention paid to issues of <a href="/wiki/Faith_healing" title="Faith healing">healing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> They have been known to follow a strict code of behaviour that dictates some of their moral beliefs and influences their actions.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Traveller children often grow up outside educational systems.<sup id="cite_ref-Garrett_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrett-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The Irish Traveller Movement, a community advocacy group, promotes equal access to education for Traveller children.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2010, the Irish Equality Tribunal ruled in favour of a traveller child in an anti-discrimination suit covering the admission practices of <a href="/wiki/CBS_High_School_Clonmel" title="CBS High School Clonmel">CBS High School Clonmel</a> in <a href="/wiki/County_Tipperary" title="County Tipperary">County Tipperary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In July 2011, the secondary school in Clonmel successfully appealed the decision of the Equality Tribunal that its admission criteria were indirectly discriminatory against children from the Traveller community.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg/220px-Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg" width="220" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg/330px-Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg/440px-Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1322" data-file-height="1300" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Tinkers_1946.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Irish Travellers in 1946</div></div></div><p>\nThe health of Irish Travellers is significantly poorer than that of the general population in Ireland. This is evidenced in a 2007 report published in Ireland, which states that over half of Travellers do not live past the age of 39 years.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Another government report of 1987 found:</p><blockquote><p>From birth to old age, they have high mortality rates, particularly from accidents, <a href="/wiki/Metabolic_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Metabolic disease">metabolic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Congenital_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Congenital disorder">congenital problems</a>, but also from other major causes of death. Female Travellers have especially high mortality compared to settled women.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health_(Ireland)" title="Department of Health (Ireland)">Department of Health and Children</a> in the Republic of Ireland, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Health,_Social_Services_and_Public_Safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Health, Social Services and Public Safety">Department of Health, Social Services and Public Safety</a> in Northern Ireland, commissioned the <a href="/wiki/University_College_Dublin" title="University College Dublin">University College Dublin</a>\'s School of Public Health and Population Science to conduct a major cross-border study of Travellers\' welfare. The study, including a detailed census of Traveller population and an examination of their health status, was expected to take up to three years to complete.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The main results of the study were published in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> of Irish Travellers has decreased since the 1990s, but they still have one of the highest birth rates in Europe. The birth rate for the Traveller community for the year 2005 was 33.32 per 1,000, possibly the highest birth rate recorded for any community in Europe.\n</p><p>On average there are ten times more driving fatalities within the Traveller community. At 22%, this represents the most common cause of death among Traveller males. Some 10% of Traveller children die before their second birthday, compared to just 1% of the general population. In Ireland, 2.6% of all deaths in the total population were for people aged under 25, versus 32% for the Travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In addition, 80% of Travellers die before the age of 65.\n</p><p>According to the National Traveller Suicide Awareness Project, Traveller men are over six times more likely to kill themselves than the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Teenage_marriage" class="mw-redirect" title="Teenage marriage">Teenage marriage</a> is common among Irish Travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-McElweeJacksonCharles2003_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McElweeJacksonCharles2003-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p110</span>)</sup> Couples tend to marry very young. According to Judith Okely, "there is no large time spans between puberty and marriage" of Travellers. Okely wrote in 1983 that the typical marriage age for females was 16\xe2\x80\x9317 and the typical marriage age for males was 18\xe2\x80\x9319.<sup id="cite_ref-Okely1983_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okely1983-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p153</span>)</sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/Census_of_Ireland_2011" title="Census of Ireland 2011">Census of Ireland 2011</a><sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the average age of an Irish Traveller was 22.4 and 52.2% were aged under 20. Yet only 252 15\xe2\x80\x9319-year-old enumerated Irish Travellers identified themselves as married.<sup id="cite_ref-ROIcensus2011_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ROIcensus2011-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_the_Environment,_Community_and_Local_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of the Environment, Community and Local Government">Department of the Environment, Community and Local Government</a> (DEHLG) in <abbr title="Republic of Ireland">ROI</abbr> "definition of a &#91;Traveller&#93; family includes unmarried Traveller men over 18 as a unit" because, according to Abdalla et al., "it is understood that they will marry at this age and require an additional unit of accommodation."<sup id="cite_ref-Abdalla2010_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abdalla2010-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Irish Travellers generally marry other Irish Travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-DOE1995_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOE1995-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p156</span>)</sup> <a href="/wiki/Consanguinity" title="Consanguinity">Consanguineous</a> marriage is common among Irish Travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-McElweeJacksonCharles2003_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McElweeJacksonCharles2003-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>pp110\xe2\x80\x93111</span>)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-DOE1995_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DOE1995-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p156</span>)</sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Irish Travellers lived as <a href="/wiki/Cohabiters" class="mw-redirect" title="Cohabiters">cohabiters</a> who "married at one time without religious or civil ceremony."<sup id="cite_ref-Griffin2008_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griffin2008-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p258</span>)</sup> Into the early 20th century about one-third of Irish Travellers were "married according to the law."<sup id="cite_ref-Griffin2008_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griffin2008-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p246</span>)</sup>\n</p><p>According to Christopher Griffin, arranged Irish Traveller marriages in the early 21st century "safeguard the girl\'s &#91;interests&#93; by securing a man who won\'t mistreat her."<sup id="cite_ref-Griffin2008_65-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Griffin2008-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p247</span>)</sup>\nAccording to <a href="/wiki/Julie_Bindel" title="Julie Bindel">Julie Bindel</a>, in <i><a href="/wiki/Standpoint_(magazine)" title="Standpoint (magazine)">Standpoint</a></i>, some Irish Traveller females in the UK are forced into marriages, but Bindel points out that data is difficult to obtain because "the line between an arranged marriage and a forced one is not always clear."<sup id="cite_ref-Bindel2012_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bindel2012-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_conflict_and_controversies">Social conflict and controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Social conflict and controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discrimination_and_prejudice">Discrimination and prejudice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Discrimination and prejudice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Travellers are often reported as the subject of explicit political and cultural discrimination, with politicians being elected on promises to block Traveller housing in local communities and individuals frequently refused service in pubs, shops and hotels.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2011 survey by the Economic and Social Research Institute of Ireland concluded that there is widespread ostracism of Travellers in Ireland, and the report concluded that it could hurt the long-term prospects for Travellers, who "need the intercultural solidarity of their neighbours in the settled community.&#160;... They are too small a minority, i.e., 0.5 percent, to survive in a meaningful manner without ongoing and supportive personal contact with their fellow citizens in the settled community."<sup id="cite_ref-Irishtimes_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irishtimes-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The general prejudice against Travellers hinders efforts by the central government to integrate Travellers into Irish society.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT102915_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT102915-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, the USA\'s <a href="/wiki/Country_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices" title="Country Reports on Human Rights Practices">Country Reports on Human Rights Practices</a> for the United Kingdom stated that Irish Travellers (among other groups) widely reported discrimination in the country, and highlighted that the High Court had ruled the government had illegally discriminated against Travellers by unlawfully subjecting planning applications to special scrutiny.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Work_and_income">Work and income</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Work and income">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>According to the 2002 Irish census, "the labour force participation rate for male Travellers (72%) slightly exceeded that for total males (70%) while the rate for female Travellers (38%) was considerably below that for females in general (47%). Unemployment among male Travellers measured 73 percent according to the self-assessed principal economic status question on the census form. The national measure of unemployment for males on a comparable basis was 9.4 per cent according to the 2002 census results. Corresponding rates for females were 63 percent for female Travellers and 8 percent for the female population overall."\n<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many Travellers are breeders of dogs such as <a href="/wiki/Greyhound" title="Greyhound">greyhounds</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lurcher" title="Lurcher">lurchers</a> and have a long-standing interest in horse trading. The main fairs associated with them are held annually at <a href="/wiki/Ballinasloe_fair" class="mw-redirect" title="Ballinasloe fair">Ballinasloe</a> (County Galway), Puck Fair (County Kerry), Ballabuidhe Horse Fair (County Cork), the twice yearly Smithfield Horse Fair (Dublin inner city) and <a href="/wiki/Appleby_Horse_Fair" title="Appleby Horse Fair">Appleby</a> (England).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> They are often involved in dealing scrap metals, e.g., 60% of the raw material for Irish steel is sourced from scrap metal, approximately 50% (75,000 metric tonnes) segregated by the community at a value of more than \xc2\xa31.5&#160;million. Such percentages for more valuable non-ferrous metals may be significantly greater.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the majority of Irish Travellers\' employment is either <a href="/wiki/Self-employment" title="Self-employment">self-employment</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wage_labour" title="Wage labour">wage labour</a>, income and financial status varies greatly from family to family. Many families choose not to reveal the specifics of their finances, but when explained it is very difficult to detect any sort of pattern or regular trend of monthly or weekly income. To detect their financial status many look to the state of the possessions: their <a href="/wiki/Travel_trailer" class="mw-redirect" title="Travel trailer">trailer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motor_vehicle" title="Motor vehicle">motor vehicle</a>, domestic utensils, and any other valuables.<sup id="cite_ref-Okely1983_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Okely1983-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p63</span>)</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_identity">Social identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Social identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Irish Travellers are recognised in <a href="/wiki/British_law" class="mw-redirect" title="British law">British law</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Law_in_the_Republic_of_Ireland" class="mw-redirect" title="Law in the Republic of Ireland">Irish law</a>, their legal status was that of a social group, until 2017. In March 2017 they were designated an Irish indigenous ethnic group.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> An ethnic group is defined as one whose members identify with each other, usually on the basis of a presumed common genealogy or ancestry. Ethnic identity is also marked by the recognition from others of a group\'s distinctiveness and by common cultural, linguistic, religious, behavioural or biological traits.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> Committee of Enquiry on Racism and <a href="/wiki/Xenophobia" title="Xenophobia">Xenophobia</a> found them to be among the most discriminated-against <a href="/wiki/Ethnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic">ethnic</a> groups in Ireland<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and yet their status remains insecure in the absence of widespread legal endorsement.<sup id="cite_ref-tinker_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinker-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Travellers are often viewed by settled people in a negative light, perceived as insular, anti-social, \'drop-outs\' and \'misfits\',<sup id="cite_ref-Hainsworth_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hainsworth-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> or believed to be involved in criminal and <a href="/wiki/Mendicant" title="Mendicant">mendicant</a> behaviour, or settling illegally on land owned by others.<sup id="cite_ref-Garrett_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Garrett-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (May 2011)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (May 2011)">not in citation given</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Violence_and_crime">Violence and crime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Violence and crime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Commission on Itinerancy, appointed in Ireland in 1960 under <a href="/wiki/Charles_Haughey" title="Charles Haughey">Charles Haughey</a>, found that "public brawling fuelled by excessive drinking further added to settled people\'s fear of Travellers&#160;... feuding was felt to be the result of a dearth of pastimes and [of] illiteracy, historically comparable to features of rural Irish life before <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">the Famine</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008 a faction fight riot broke out in D\'Alton Park, <a href="/wiki/Mullingar" title="Mullingar">Mullingar</a> involving up to 65 people of the <a href="/wiki/Nevin_(surname)" title="Nevin (surname)">Nevin</a>, Dinnegan and McDonagh families. The court hearing in 2010 resulted in suspended sentences for all the defendants.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The cause may have been an unpaid gambling debt linked to a <a href="/wiki/Bare-knuckle_boxing" title="Bare-knuckle boxing">bare-knuckle boxing</a> match.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 2011 report, conducted by the Irish Chaplaincy in Britain, <i>Voices Unheard: A Study of Irish Travellers in Prison</i> (Mac Gabhann, 2011) found that social, economic and educational exclusion were contributing factors to the "increasingly high levels of imprisonment" of Irish Travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, Irish Travelers from the <a href="/wiki/South_Atlantic_states" title="South Atlantic states">southern east coast</a> of the United States plead guilty to charges of perpetrated scams on homeowners as well as government agencies. By 2017, 52 had plead guilty to violations of the federal <a href="/wiki/Racketeer_Influenced_and_Corrupt_Organizations_Act" title="Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act">Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act</a> (RICO).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_disputes">Land disputes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Land disputes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Halting_site" title="Halting site">Halting site</a></div>\n<p>A complaint against Travellers in the United Kingdom is that of unauthorised Traveller sites being established on privately owned land or on council-owned land not designated for that purpose. Under the government\'s "<i>Gypsy and Traveller Sites Grant</i>", designated sites for Travellers\' use are provided by councils, and funds are made available to local authorities for the construction of new sites and maintenance and extension of existing sites.\n</p><p>However, Travellers also frequently make use of other, non-authorised sites, including public "<a href="/wiki/Common_land" title="Common land">common land</a>" and private plots such as large fields and other privately-owned land. A famous example was <a href="/wiki/Dale_Farm" title="Dale Farm">Dale Farm</a> in Essex. The Travellers claim that there is an under-provision of authorised sites. The Gypsy Council estimates an under-provision amounts to insufficient sites for 3,500 people.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> \n</p><p>The passing of the <a href="/wiki/Caravan_Sites_Act_1968" title="Caravan Sites Act 1968">Caravan Sites Act 1968</a>, for some time, safeguarded their right to a site, but the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Justice_and_Public_Order_Act_1994" title="Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994">Criminal Justice and Public Order Act 1994</a> repealed part II of the 1968 act, removing the duty on local authorities in the UK to provide sites for Travellers and giving them the power to close down existing sites. In Northern Ireland, opposition to Travellers\' sites has been led by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Unionist_Party" title="Democratic Unionist Party">Democratic Unionist Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hainsworth_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hainsworth-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="List_of_Travellers.27_organisations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_Travellers\'_organisations">List of Travellers\' organisations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: List of Travellers&#039; organisations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg/220px-Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg.png" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg/330px-Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg/440px-Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="759" data-file-height="496" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Irish_Traveller_Movement_flag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The flag of the Irish Traveller Movement<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The following are some of the Travellers\' representative organisations formed since the 1960s:<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Irish Traveller Community (1960s)</li>\n<li>Itinerant Settlement Committee (1960s\xe2\x80\x931980s)</li>\n<li>Travellers\' Rights Committee (1981\xe2\x80\x9383)</li>\n<li>Minceir Misli (1983\xe2\x80\x9385)</li>\n<li>Travellers\' Education and Development Group (founded in 1984)</li>\n<li>Pavee Point (founded 1985)<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Irish Travellers\' Movement (founded in 1990)</li>\n<li>Cork Traveller Visibility Group Ltd. (founded early 1990\'s)<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/National_Traveller_Women%27s_Forum" title="National Traveller Women&#39;s Forum">National Traveller Women\'s Forum</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Depictions_and_documentaries">Depictions and documentaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Depictions and documentaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Irish_Traveller-related_depictions_and_documentaries" title="List of Irish Traveller-related depictions and documentaries">List of Irish Traveller-related depictions and documentaries</a></div>\n<p>Irish Travellers have been depicted, usually negatively but sometimes with some care and sympathy, in film, radio, print, and television. Shows like <i><a href="/wiki/The_Riches" title="The Riches">The Riches</a></i> (2007\xe2\x80\x932008), the American television series featuring <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Izzard" title="Eddie Izzard">Eddie Izzard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Driver" title="Minnie Driver">Minnie Driver</a>, take a deeper look into the Traveller lifestyle. More recently, the documentary series <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Fat_Gypsy_Weddings" title="Big Fat Gypsy Weddings">Big Fat Gypsy Weddings</a></i> (2010, 2011, and 2012) has been commercially successful in the United Kingdom, offering glimpses of Traveller life as viewed at real-life weddings. A 1997 American film, <i><a href="/wiki/Traveller_(1997_film)" title="Traveller (1997 film)">Traveller</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Bill_Paxton" title="Bill Paxton">Bill Paxton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Wahlberg" title="Mark Wahlberg">Mark Wahlberg</a>, also explored the Travellers in America.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_Travellers&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/32px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/48px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/64px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:United_Kingdom" title="Portal:United Kingdom">United Kingdom portal</a></span></li>\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Four_Provinces_Flag.svg/32px-Four_Provinces_Flag.svg.png" width="32" height="16" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Four_Provinces_Flag.svg/48px-Four_Provinces_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-64">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A 1986 study reported that 39% of marriages in the study were between first cousins.<sup id="cite_ref-McElweeJacksonCharles2003_60-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McElweeJacksonCharles2003-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">(<span>p110</span>)</sup> According to Alison Healy in 2003, 19\xe2\x80\x9340% of Irish Traveller marriages are between first cousins.<sup id="cite_ref-Healy2003_63-0" class="reference"><a
